We must ensure that that lady, a member of our community, is able to receive the attention that she deserves, so tomorrow morning I will be asking this place that we consider a notice of motion to be debated next year about an independent inquiry for Sue Neill-Fraser. I am sending that to you now - I wasn't going to - so you have time to think about this overnight from the evidence you've heard and from what we know.

I thank all those who have contributed to this debate.

It is confronting to be faced with evidence that our expectations have not been met. It requires us all to move from a comfortable belief that all is well to the unpleasant realisation that serious mistakes were made, the cumulative effect of which is a miscarriage of justice.

In the Sue Neill-Fraser case, the totality of the evidence gathered from police, RTI disclosures, analysis of past and recent scientific advances and the work of lawyer Etter and barrister Hugh Selby over many years means that we've moved beyond suspicions that not all is well to the certainty that the government must move quickly to bring her case before the Court of Criminal Appeal.

I should also comment the last time I raised the Selby issue some years ago, I arrived home that night after being here presenting. I usually don't answer phone calls that are private or unknown, but I did. I had a pen and paper there. I had this voice, and the voice said to me, 'Are you that Gaffney fella?' and I said, 'Yes, that's me.' he said, 'Are you the one who's just done this Sue Neill-Fraser thing at that parliament?', I said 'Yes' and he said 'Well, I've got something I need to tell you' and he gave the name of a person who he said his girlfriend had known was the killer of Bob Chappell. My response, and I've not mentioned this to anybody else, but I think this is how important I believe this is to be - I rang the commissioner who was Darren Hine at the time and I said, 'This is the phone call, this is what I've received, what do I do?' and he said somebody will ring you within five minutes and that happened. I feel that is important information because that name was given to me and the police were aware of that name.

In closing, it is telling that in the near three weeks since I tabled the Etter-Selby report that there has been science from the police and the ODPP. It is telling not only because they may have no answer, it is also telling because being able to own up to a mistake is one of the hardest things to do. Rather than belatedly joining in a quest for truth and justice, the latest example of bunkering down is the police RTI response last week to the member Meg Webb, refusing to disclose the full exchange of Dr Duncan Taylor, of Forensics South Australia that predates the 2021 appeal. In the face of such determined intransigence and a commitment to keeping the lid on, there's only one solution I believe, a wide-ranging powerful commission of inquiry so that this matter can be fully resolved. I move my notice of motion.

Motion agreed to.

[10.43 p.m.]
Mr DUIGAN (Windermere - Minister for Sport) - Mr President, I thank the Chamber for its indulgence. I'd like to make a clarifying statement on answers I gave in both budget Estimates and in the House of Assembly this morning. In answer to a question from Mr Winter in budget Estimates, I said the following: [tbc 10.42]

I believe Mr Hall shortly after I sent him that letter went out and stood next to you, as you provided an alternative for him. On the basis of that, I chose not to sign my letter.

On reflection, I should have clarified that what I meant by this was that I didn't sign the letter on the basis that the club had made clear they had an alternate proposal to the one we had been discussing, and the one I had articulated in my draft letter to the president.

It was not my intention in my actions during the campaign, nor in the statements I've made since, that I didn't sign the letter because Mr Hall stood with Mr Winter during the campaign. It was, as I have said in the media appearance, the club clearly indicated it had a preference for a particular course of action that wasn't reflected in the draft letter I had sent to the president.

I regret that my answers may have given the North Launceston Football Club or the public the impression that I would seek to punish the club in the decisions I make for meeting with other members of parliament, as is their clear right. My absolute focus is to find an outcome for the club that is mutually agreeable and beneficial. Again, I thank the Chamber for its indulgence.

The Council adjourned at 10.44 p.m.
